but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但烏托爾斯•曼明尼爾斯•曼明尼爾斯 , 你聽到這段時間的歷史 , 在19世紀的歷史中 , 你聽到這段時間的歷史 , 很久以前 , 我們就開始了 , 直到我們要去到一個更近的時刻 , 來到我們身邊的機會 , 來到我們身邊 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	通常 , 這些人常常見過血液、女士、女士、女士 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	而我的信息是 , 我相信我們會被認為 , 正如你所知的 , 世界的新力量 , 正開始改變和世界的新力量 , 正開始改變和新的力量 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是我們現在看到的 , 非常顯然的 , 通常是很顯然的 , 通常都是非常強烈的 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 它發生了每一世紀 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭議 , 當權力從古老的國家開始 , 歐洲大西洋的新興起 , 歐洲大西洋 , 歐洲大西洋的新興起 , 歐洲大西洋的新興起 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在大戰中 , 二次世界大戰時 , 大戰的大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	馬諾•西里斯對他們來說 , 這可能是比較準確的描述他們 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在這個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 第一件事是關於改變權力 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二點是關於一些新維度 , 我想要提到的 , 現在它已經發生了 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	咱們來談談關於權力的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事是 , 有一種感覺 , 因為它從未發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到了一些微妙的改變 , 在歐洲文明的權力轉變 , 但我們看到了一些不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅僅僅僅是從國內搬到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也動作了 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	今天的情況是 , 在國際階段 , 國際階段的權力是被強大的 , 以至於全球階段的力量 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化的全球化 , 但實際上是全球化的全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	而在國際階段的情況下 , 國際階段的規則是不夠的 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球階段的力量 , 目前正在發展預算的力量 , 像是金融管理器的力量 , 將我們帶到金融監控器的力量 , 如今 , 國際階段和全球階段的力量 , 大約是302倍的力量 , 如我們所知 , 金融管理器的力量 , 使我們在金融的限制中 , 使我們更大量金融的力量 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球空間的空間中 , 沒有任何規律的規則 , 不管是法律的規則 , 不管是法律的規則 , 人們可能會自由的限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 讓它變得很強大 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	不需要國際貿易、網際貿易、網際貿易、網際貿易、網際貿易、網際貿易、網際網路等等 , 但 , 不管你想要國際貿易、國際貿易、網路等等 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11事件 , 即使你是最強大的國家 , 甚至是地球上最強大的國家 , 不管你是地球上最強大的城市之一 , 你甚至是在地球上最強大的城市之一 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	大約有60%的9/11摧毀了 , 9/11摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看到 , 我們的敵人也使用這個空間的空間 , 網路 , 衛星廣播 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間的空間 , 來追蹤我們的系統和我們的系統 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久之後 , 歷史的規則是權力管理局的規則 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	假如我相信它是全球化的力量 , 那麼它會追蹤我們時代的挑戰之一 , 就是要帶領國際空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 數十年來 , 我們都能夠達成目標 , 不管我們能達成目標的目標 , 或更少 , 或更少的機會 , 才能達成目標 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	注意到 , 我不是談論政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在討論一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	我自己的看法 , 各位 , 各位先生 , 女士和glemen , 不太可能是這樣 , 不用於美國國制度 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有美國國家 , 我們就必須發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要國際援助 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個意義 , 就是你可以合法國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當它進入國際空間時 , 我猜測並不會發生在世界各地的國際空間中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會被強大的合理化合成 , 以基礎系統、治療基礎系統 , 來治療基礎系統 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織 , 聯合國 , 聯合國 , 聯合國 , 卻有強大的力量 , 甚至是最強大的 , 不管是誰 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:他們開始試圖創造一個治療基礎組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們知道現在我們必須把一個機構分配給財務管理 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是g20的基礎機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們會回來想想 , 如果你把最強大的規則 , 把最強大的規則放在治療基礎機構上 , 那麼 , 會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們會再回到它 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一條訊息是 , 如果你要通過這些多數量 , 或更少的機會 , 那麼我們就成功了 , 以確保我們的能力 , 來確保我們的能力 , 來確保我們的能力 , 來確保我們的能力 , 來確保我們的能力 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看看這開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和觀眾談話 , 但權力不只是轉變 , 而是改變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說故事 , 歷史文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史文明 , 在西方國家的歷史文明中海中海中海中海中海中海中海中海中海岸 , 更近期的西方國家 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	似乎我覺得我們現在看到一個基本的轉變 , 讓國家聚集在太平洋的河岸上 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	從經濟權力開始 , 但它總是開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到發展國家的發展能力 , 國政策略 , 將其它成長的國家發展出來 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為事實上這不是從西洋到東部的轉變 , 有些不同發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 在接下來的十年中 , 美國的國家將會保持最強大的國家 , 但在接下來的十年 , 十年後 , 美國的國家將會保持最強大的國家 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們在50年間 , 最不尋常的情況下 , 不論是在哪裡 , 我們都擁有了一台巨大的機制 , 不論是在哪裡 , 不管是哪個國家 , 或對抗的速度 , 都不得不平衡 , 以至於世界上最不尋常的情況 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是典型的歷史 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在 , 正常的情況是歷史上 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多世界的新興 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國已經成為我們世界的特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家 , 但他們會成為世界上最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	當然 , 你可以看到中國的中心 , 當然 , 我自己的猜測是中國 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測是中國 , 當然 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測不是平面 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	在自由化經濟時 , 民主化的社會自由化了她的經濟 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是一個不同的討論 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	看來 , 歐洲人更像歐洲 , 歐洲人在十九世紀的歐洲人越來越多 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	在19世紀:一個偉大的英國國王國王國 , 叫做歐洲的 「 歐洲警察 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	平衡是平衡的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林一起合作 , 英國和柏林一起合作 , 聯合國 , 英國人和柏林一起合作 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在 , 注意到 , 在一個巨大的世界中 , 你有解決方案 , 包括 「 警察世界 」 , 你有解決方案 , 包括 「 警察 」 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	權力的力量意味著解決方案 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但有多種力量的力量意味著轉變和改變 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們所在的世界 , 我們會越來越清楚地發現我們的盟友不是解決的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	英國外國人說: 「 英國外國人很常見 , 但沒有共同的利益 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會發現 , 若我們想要在世界各地的大西洋棋盤上 , 我們就會發現 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	不 , 我們不夠好 , 不夠好 , 我們必須把他人放進去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須在這個案例中 , 阿拉伯同事 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我認為伊拉克和阿富汗是伊拉克和阿富汗的最後一次 , 我們沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜是 , 西方國家有四百年來 , 我們就開始了 , 因為它是西方國家的基礎 , 和西方國家的基礎 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方人都可以在世界各地的角度找到它的聯繫 。
but that's no longer true .	但這不再是真的 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	在第二次世界大戰結束後 ,
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行 , 國際銀行 , 國際銀行 , 國際銀行 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給其他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造出20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在 , 我們必須超越我們西方朋友的困境 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你做預測 , 可能更有趣 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經達到了400年 , 當西方權力夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會把自己帶在世界各地 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	噢 , 是的 , 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國的藍色旗子在藍色的藍色旗下 , 保留在藍色的旗幟上 , 在藍色旗幟上 , 保留在藍色的美國國家 。
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大的敘述馬里斯塔克馬里斯呢 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的文字
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是一家餐廳 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要保持海平線 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	此刻 , 我們要和我們分享價值的人 , 但我們共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的不同的角度來看世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	這是第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	在現代世界中 , 我們的現代世界 , 因為網路 , 因為網路 , 因為網路 , 因為網路 , 因為人們所說的 , 一切都和一切有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是獨立的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在已經被阻擋了 , 像是國家一樣 , 以前從來沒有過過這樣的情況 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家的聯繫 , 它總是存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交人是國際關係的國際關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們非常緊密在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥 , 加油機場有24個小時 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	lehman兄弟走進 , 整個大崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯的火焰中 , 非洲有火焰 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們深深深深地深深地深深地深深地連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 國家和其他人之間的聯繫 , 而不是與其他人合作 , 而非與其他人聯繫 , 而非與其他人聯繫 , 而非與其他人聯繫 , 而非與其他人合作 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為在國內的國家不再是國家的力量 , 因為在國際國家的行動中 , 國家的影響會發生在國內的影響 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家有強大的力量 , 強壯的是我們的軍隊 , 強壯的是我們的軍隊 , 強壯的武器 , 我們的軍隊 , 強壯的武器 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那就是當敵人在牆壁上時 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在的敵人在牆壁上 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想要談談我的國家 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 因為糧食安全是我的國家 , 因為糧食安全是威脅我的國家 , 因為糧食安全和我國內的警察 , 我必須談談我的國防部 , 因為食物安全 , 我必須跟大家談談我們的敵人 , 因為糧食安全感染了我的國家 , 因為糧食安全和我國內的警察 , 我必須談談我們的敵人 , 因為糧食安全感染了我的國家 , 因為糧食安全和我國內的醫療保障 , 我必須說 , 對於我們的敵人來說 , 我們的確保證了我國內的警察 , 我必須說 , 對於我們的敵人來說 , 我們的健康是從網路戰爭中所見到的 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	國家的安全並不是一個國家的安全性 , 僅僅僅僅是為了它的安全 , 和國防部的安全 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它可以阻止它的機構 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你們一些很重要的事情 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴各位 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式 , 基本上 , 建構在工業革命上 , 基本上 , 建構了 , 基本上 , 基本上都是錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業知識中 , 我們的時代 , 女士和glemen是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你的政府和外面的能力 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是第三個法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便一提 , 別問我 , 別問我 , 不要問我 , 因為我沒有發明 , 但它總是聽起來更好 , 如果有第三個法律 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三個法律就是在現代時代 , 所有東西都和其他人有關 , 你所能做的是 , 最重要的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是你是政府 , 你不管你是政府 , 不管你是政府 , 不管你是政府 , 不管你是政府 , 不管你是政府 , 不管你是政府 , 不管你是政府 , 不管你是誰 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你知道在工業上 , 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事情 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是例子 , 女士和女士們 , 我們現在都在這個情況下 , 先前和各位分享 , 先前的例子 , 先生 , 也是我們共同的情況 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 最初期的概念是 , 保持我們的國家 , 不再夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我安全 , 比他們的國家更強大 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是這樣 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	聯合國和敵人之間的聯繫 , 和敵人之間的聯繫 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	在1970年代 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和蘇聯結合在一起 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和蘇聯結合在一起 。
collective security is not enough .	收集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平對北愛爾蘭因為兩方都意識到 , 因為雙方都無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人的敵人有敵人 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東地區最好的障礙 , 就是雙方都是雙方 , 和平在中東 , 不了解他們和平的障礙是兩者 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 突然間 , 女士和女士們都在公共政策上 , 我們必須認真是公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從首詩開始 , 我終於一首詩 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐妮的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 寄給誰是酒吧 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	詩叫 「 沒有人是個島嶼 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個人死亡都會影響我 。 」 「 人類的死亡都會影響我 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰尼 , 道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們而言 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	去年紀年紀年紀念碑 , 以 「 藍色區域 」 和 「 藍色區域 」 的居民住在tedxtc , 他分享了9個共同的飲食和生命生活方式 , 來記錄在tedxttersetner和團隊研究世界的藍色區域 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	丹佛•布雷特:如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一名叫dnadanetwin研究的證據顯示 , 只有大約10%的壽命 , 在某些生物限制中 , 我們的基因 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他90%被我們的生活方式 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	藍色區塊:如果我們能找到最佳的生活方式 , 我們能找到最佳的生活方式 , 可以找到最佳的生活方式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人最樂觀的平均壽命 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	牠們可能聽過南海灘飲食或飲食
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐巴爾告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生奧茲告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重要的是 , 許多困惑可以幫助我們更好的生活 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松或做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃牛肉 , 或應該吃肉嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	到供應 , 你應該要帶他們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或resveratrmons呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是要扮演嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性呢 ? 我們如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們的國家地理地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理地地理
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶一個團隊專家 , 去了解這些人在哪裡 , 去除非文化歧視 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後 , 我會告訴各位 , 究竟是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想要破壞一些共同的迷思 , 來到長久以來 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個神話是如果你試著真的很難活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 只有一萬五千人住在美國生活中有五千人 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使這是美國最快的人口統計 , 但很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有計畫長壽 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被稱為 「 成功的成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒我我的大學 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 年齡 」 , 你的孩子有孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在演化的過程中 , 演化完全失望 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是個哺乳類動物 , 如果你是個哺乳類動物 , 如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是個哺乳類動物 , 如果你是哺乳類動物 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	為了要讓這一百人 , 你還不需要有很好的生活方式 , 你也必須有更好的生活方式 , 你也必須有非常好的生活方式 , 你也必須有更好的生活方式 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助慢慢、逆轉或甚至停止 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 會有9999個東西可以帶給我們 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	幾分鐘的大腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩樂團在你的膝蓋上 , 你的膝蓋 , 你的膝蓋 , 沒有回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的大腦可以把大腦連結起來 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	只有太多問題了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆兆個細胞 , 和 「 t 」 。 我們在討論國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就已經超過一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己丟掉 , 就會造成傷害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它也建構了數量 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像我們花了幾天的時間 , 會讓我們的朋友複製 , 很快地 , 會讓我們的朋友複製 , 很快地 , 會讓我們的朋友複製 , 很快地 , 會讓我們的朋友複製 , 像是 「 聽起來 」 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼65歲的人比112歲的速度比12歲的人更快 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果有沒有什麼可以做些什麼 ? 你還是停止你的衰老 , 我在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	重要的是 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 對於人類身體而言 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 你的身體是最好的 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這國家的壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線上 , 我們已經留了大約12個好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們可以做到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 他們會很慢性疾病、心臟病、心臟疾病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法就是去看看文化在這個國家中產出的數年 , 數年以來 , 數年以來的人口數量增加了10倍 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一條藍色區塊 , 大約125英里 , 在海岸的海岸 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 只有1.4萬人 , 但在高地 , 島嶼是大約1.4萬人 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有這個區域 , 比美國最長的10倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只能達成百分之十 , 他們做了非常多的特性 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 有102歲的年輕人 , 比他們更年輕 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回到了基督的歷史 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是布朗西的文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是很大的 , 它們大量是大量的 , 它們大量的地位 , 大量的地位 , 它們大量的 , 大量的 , 大量的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食是非常植物的 , 牠們的食物可以帶著食物 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	牠們來源於 「 香草動物 」 和 「 牛肉 」 的種類 , 像是 「 香草動物 」 和 「 牛肉 」 的種類 , 和 「 牛肉動物 」 一樣 , 有三次大量的葡萄牙 , 和 「 牛肉 」 的 「 大量 」 的味道 , 比任何世界各地的廚師都有三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密就是他們組織社會的秘密 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩利尼亞社會的其中之一是他們治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎是24歲嗎 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在沙尼亞 , 你得到越多的智慧 , 你越多的智慧 , 才能得到更多的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你在薩斯維納州的海岸線上看運動 , 看到了西洋棋的口號 , 不是看過西洋棋的路線 , 你看到了西洋棋的運動 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 不只對你的父母親戚父母保持他們的家庭 , 比例來說 , 比例來說 , 比例來說 , 比較低的家庭 , 大約有四到六年的死亡率 , 和低於死亡率的差異 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效果 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現我們的第二個藍色區塊 , 大約是八百英里的南雅 , 海岸的邊緣 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在北部地區的北部地區 , 它是陸地的北極洲 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是一個地方 , 最古老的居民族群已經發現了 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	人類是世界上最長壽命的壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你們 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你們 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你們 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你們 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人更長壽 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	美國有十五分之一的乳癌、乳癌和乳癌 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化的確有了這些數字 , 讓它能教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物的飲食和許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了八倍的美國人 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種各式各樣的策略 , 來保持在美國 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到最少的策略:它們吃掉少數的策略 , 所以他們會吃少數的策略 , 通常會吃少數的策略 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不是保守家庭風格 , 把食物帶到桌上 , 把食物帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們有三千歲的老年人 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它被發明了 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那個飲食被稱為 「 哈拉 」 、 「 哈拉 」 和 「 哈拉 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	只是一個簡單的說法 , 只能提醒他們停止吃食物 , 只能提醒他們停止吃三分之八十 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它花了一半小時的時間從你的腦袋傳送到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住你要停止80%的幫助 , 讓你們做得很不錯 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但是 , 像沙尼亞 , okinia , okinia , okinia和長壽的社會建議有關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道暴力殺害 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五年前 , 平均美國有三個朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 你出生 , 你生進了一個系統 , 你生出生 , 你出生 , 你出生 , 你出生 , 你出生 , 你出生 , 你出生了一半十個朋友 , 你就出生了 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為 「 媽媽 」 , 如果你有了你的回憶 , 你總是有著你的回憶 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這些五個女士已經開始了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們將成年人的生活分成兩段 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 通常會把椅子往往亞里薩到亞里桑達 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan的語言中 , 甚至沒有 「 退休 」 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	換句話是 「 英文字 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	早上醒來的原因是 「 早上醒來的原因 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位102歲的凱特•馬斯特 , 他的志工智慧是將它結合起來的 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這個百歲的漁民而言 , 漁民的漁民在一週三次就要捕魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 美國國家的研究人員也給了我們一個問題 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是非常文化的 , 人們會問這個問題 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你在哪裡 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們早上就知道為什麼他們在早上 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這個102歲的女士來說 , 她的祖母 , 她的祖母是她的祖母 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩分離在101年半年 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 有什麼感覺 , 希望她能強烈的感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回頭回頭說: 「 感覺就像爬進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯地理想我找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	為了我們觀察到達尼蘇達的百分之二 , 實際上 , 那裡有非常高的進展 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們轉變了數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長的壽命 , 加州 , 加州 , 加州 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	保守主義者是保守派的 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們在星期五星期六的天空 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時聖經》 , 他們稱它為 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循了五個小習慣 , 說話 , 比較不平凡 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但 , 她們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差不多的情況是 , 那些預期會超過美國人的預期壽命 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這是一項研究 , 大約有七萬人 , 三十年來 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	調查研究 , 我覺得這藍色區域的確保證了這個藍色區域 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個獨立的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、伊斯蘭人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	牠們唯一的共同點是一組非常小的生命 , 通常都是一群非常小的生命 , 牠們通常都是一群非常小的生命 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們把他們的飲食直接從聖經中 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因s:chpter , 上帝談論的是綠色植物 , 上帝談論的是綠色植物 , 上帝談論的是綠色植物 , 不可思議 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們把這條時間非常嚴肅 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每星期24小時 , 他們都停止一切 , 不管他們在哪裡工作 , 他們停下來 , 不管他們是多麼忙碌 , 他們會停止一切 , 他們會停止一切 , 他們停止一切 , 關心在他們的上帝、社交網路 , 不管他們是多麼忙碌 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這不是它的運作方式 , 權力是每週一生都在做 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有錢 , 不需要錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	倡議員也傾向與其他的援助 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去一個倡議員黨派你不會看到人們在喜愛的黨派 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們祈禱 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但他們會影響彼此的影響 , 更深深的影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化的文化 , 充滿了黃色的價值 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	伊爾•威爾斯塔是97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個多數百萬美元 , 他是多數英鎊 , 他說: 「 這樣我才能建造一個隱私的金錢 , 我會這樣做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天 , 他穿著穿透鏡頭 , 穿著垃圾 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的是 , 或許 , 在手術室裡的第四天 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在旁邊的傢伙 , 打開了手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97年 , 他仍有20公開的手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	早上 , 十三歲 , 一隻游泳 , 牠早上醒來 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	他喜歡把紙板放進板上 , 把板子丟進去 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的祖母住在那座城市中 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她開始了她每天的軟體 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她還在1994年的阿伯納諾•安德魯斯•蓋爾 , 在那裡 , 她仍自願參與了七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在19個難以置信了 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能只是你見過的人 , 他在薩哈拉沙哈拉沙哈拉沙哈拉沙哈拉沙哈拉沙漠 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我會告訴你們 , 沒有冒險的傷害 , 沒有任何冒險比起飛機的火車 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是個朋友我還沒見過 , 但她會告訴我 。 」
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這些三文化的共同點子是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都做過什麼事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	然後我們就把它放到9 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經做了兩種藍色區塊 , 而這些常見的偏見 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我要注意到這一點 , 不是他們運動 , 至少我們認為練習 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 它們會不斷地不斷地進入身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些100歲的男孩 , 她們坐在地上 , 她們坐在地板上 , 她們坐在地上 , 她們坐在地面上 , 每天都坐在地上 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	sardiniansardiniansardiniansardinian住在垂直的樓梯上
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟旅程 , 或是教堂或朋友的家店 , 都會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何意見 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做法律或家工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們就這樣做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒的卡路里 , 就如同在座的卡路里一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們這麼做時 , 他們都會傾向走路 , 唯一能證明的原因是 , 他們會傾向走進去 , 正面臨界線上 , 正是他們享受的經驗 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何在正確的路上找到他們的生活方式 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	這些文化都需要時間轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	sardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardinians
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這個祖先的祖先 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在傷害或壓力時 , 它會引發一種稱為 「 感染性疾病 」 的疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你慢慢在十五分鐘的時間內 , 就會變成更反的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有了 「 軟體 」 的詞彙 , 像是 「 okinawa 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你們知道在人生中最危險的一年 , 一年後 , 你每年都會退休 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們生命的意義 , 他們活在人生中 , 他們活在他們的人生中 , 花了七年的時間 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一點一點 , 不是很難賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是大豆和甜甜 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	它們有策略 , 使它們從桌子上升到不穩定 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	結果就是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把他們的孩子和他們的孩子帶著他們的孩子 , 去照顧他們的孩子 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於信仰基礎的社群 , 值得4.4倍的壽命 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最棒的是他們也屬於右邊的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生出生 , 或他們正處於對人的身邊 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們知道 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友是肥胖症 , 如果你三個比較好的朋友是肥胖的機率 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你從不健康的人身上 , 就會有很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友的思想 , 你的信任和信任信任 , 你的朋友的意願是真實的活動 , 但不是太多 , 或花園 , 如果你朋友的思想 , 你的信任和信任 , 你的確保持了 , 不管你是怎樣的 , 他們會對抗 , 很大的影響力 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食並不是工作 , 不是工作 , 全世界的人口數量超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動程式通常是在日年1月中 , 他們通常都在月球上 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當它不再短暫時 , 沒有短期的規律 , 或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想想看 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 可能是最重要的事情 , 你就可以花了幾年的時間 , 來做更多年的時間 , 你的生命 , 和你的朋友長期冒險 。 謝謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	基本上 , 它的確是用它來源頭的 , 來源於它 , 讓它開始玩耍 , 讓它變得很棒 , 我們會發現它們是如何運作的 , 和酷的新材料 , 我們會發現它們是如何運作的 , 和酷的新材料 , 我們會發現它們是如何運作的 , 很棒的 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	卡塔里娜•莫塔:玩有聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一位朋友在葡萄牙 , 他可以運送他的家人 , 他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他因爲他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有時候我們了解到如何運作 , 或 , 我們可以建立和修復它們 , 這樣我們就可以建立和修復它們 , 或至少能建立和修復它們 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀中 , 許多這些創業人都失敗了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 建築師社群和開放原始碼來源於我們的生活 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶進我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶進我們的生活中 , 讓它們變成我們的生活 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統材料是如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人的塑膠 , 那些改變形狀的塑膠 , 會改變形狀 , 顏色的塑膠 , 會產生電力 , 顏色 , 製造電力 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我展示一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	用傳統的印刷電路板或電路線 , 不用傳統印刷電路或線線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個感應器 , 用它來產生觸感感應器對我的皮膚產生感應器 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	專家使用它在雷射印刷和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一顆粒子 , 用顏色光明的粒子來源 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 當一般的光線繞著整個表面時 , 我會把光線轉移到外面 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	其中兩種的應用程式 , 包括內部的應用程式 , 包括神經系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	氣候變遷會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱點上 , 讓它的溫度更高 , 你可以看到它會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶子裡 , 牠會發現 , 當內容變得很酷的時候 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅少數人所知的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年來 , 他們會在日常生活中使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行器 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 改變顏色依賴於溫度、鍵盤 , 和風扇 , 可以改變顏色 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一位社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要談的是智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是作家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很擅長了解它們如何運作 , 但也是因為我相信我們應該有更深的了解 , 來創造我們的世界 , 而現在 , 我們並不知道這些高科技的成果是如何運作的 , 因為我相信我們應該有更深的了解 , 來創造我們未來的成果 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	聰明的材料很難取得小量子 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以使用它們 , 非常小說它們是如何使用它們 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 大部分都是在貿易秘密和專利的專利中 , 他們就存在於貿易秘密和專利 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 我開始了一個計畫叫做 「 開材 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們也想加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們會喜歡它成為大型的資料庫 , 集體在智慧材料中產生資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但是為什麼我們要照顧聰明材料和它們所組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的 , 而我們不了解 , 以及我們不了解的事物 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品 , 包括我們的生活、健康和品質生活的物品 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們生活在一個世界聰明的材料中 , 我們應該知道它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 重要的是 , 創新一直都被推動者 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	許多時候 , 不專家 , 專家 , 專家 , 不是專家 , 而是從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學非常複雜 , 需要昂貴的裝置 。
but that's not always the case .	但這不是總是這樣 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	兩位科學家在艾利諾斯學院發現 , 他們發表了一篇文字 , 用簡單的方法來製造出版 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbardanbunker , 他沒有任何經驗 , 直到 , 讀這篇論文和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了阿密克斯特的發明 , 他用了阿密克斯特 , 他甚至製造了自己的軟體 , 同時 , 他甚至創造了自己的軟體 , 甚至製造了自己的軟體 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	jordan在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括所有他嘗試過的結果 , 沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究和改善它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以jordan的主要創新是要把一個實驗放在芝加哥的實驗室裡 , 讓他自己做一個實驗 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他出版了這份工作 , 其他人可以選出一個更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我想提到她計畫的目標是要提高高速的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 他們教導我們如何運作 , 但對他們教導我們如何運作的事物 , 但它的影響方式是如何運作的 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的作品是建立一個技巧 , 來創造出獨特的技巧 , 來創造出獨特的技巧 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來創造出不尋常的事物 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[報紙]我們看到的是一張紙張紙張貼在紙上 , 和磁鐵一樣 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以基於來自mit.漢娜創造了一系列的論文 , 漢娜創造了一系列的論文 , 漢娜創造了一系列的論文 , 漢娜創造了一系列的論文 , 漢娜創造了一系列的論文 , 漢娜創造了一系列的論文 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	像jordan和其他作家一樣 , 漢娜會讓任何人複製 , 讓任何人能複製它 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是其中之一 , 它讓我們能夠創造更便宜且有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜•阿富汗娜的創作 , 她分享了她的發現 , 開放了新的可能性 , 同時 , 新可能性 , 和創新的可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	有趣的是 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 我們不會害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常處理問題 , 從未預期的角度來看 , 在過程中 , 最終發現了解決方案 , 或更好的方法 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 更多研究人員願意分享他們的知識 , 更好的機會 , 我們需要創造科技的機會 , 才能分享他們的知識 , 更好的機會 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我感覺到1970年代初期 , 他寫了: 「 你必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主導 , 沒有一個夢想在家裡 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你必須要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住我們在未來的知識中 , 能確保我們有所謂的知識 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會看到幾台車輛 , 用預測模式來計算安全的路徑 , 用預測模式來計算安全的路徑 , 用預測模式 , 來計算安全的路徑 , 讓每個人在路邊的路上 , 不意外地 , 不用意外 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛:如果車禍可能會避免 , 可能會避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們面對:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	我們不喜歡去思考這個事實 , 但事實證明我們知道這個事實是真實的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是死於死亡率和75%的死亡率 , 不用藥品或酒吧 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說 , 但我記得我的第一個意見 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上開車站在高速公路上 , 我看到了車輛 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢慢 , 我會慢慢 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上腳踏車
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 這傢伙並不慢慢 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停止死停 , 停止死亡停止 , 停止死亡停止 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在布拉克 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我知道它不會停止 , 我知道它不會停止 , 我知道它不會停止 , 我知道它不會停止 , 車子會停下來 , 車子會停下來 , 車子會停止 , 空氣袋子都停下來 , 不停地 , 車子會停止 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道汽車停止了 , 我認為我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛的經驗 , 讓車輛和彼此溝通 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們能想像一下現在的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車 , 你在玻璃泡泡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個極端的身體中 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你在高速公路的路線上移動 , 並且在超人類的速度下降 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你必須指導你的兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這是你所做的第一件事 , 他們問你要做些什麼 , 但你會問你怎麼做 , 不是真的設計這個任務 , 但你會問你怎麼做 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放在路上 , 這是正確的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看看你正在走路 , 然後開車走路 , 不要在路上走路 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人都是安全的 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 來看看嗎 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會在路上走路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶然我們會錯過一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們覺得太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 駕駛者說: 「 我沒看到它 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得見 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在可以幫助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車輛和車輛相互相同 , 我們會看到三輛車輛 , 車輛和車輛相同 , 我們會看到不只三台車子 , 和左邊 , 我們會看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們可以看到這輛車輛的車輛在我們面前 , 看看速度是多快 , 或停下來 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙會走到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	根據計算和預測模式 , 我們將會看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	真的 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維空間的物體 , 可以修復和重視 。
they travel down roads .	他們走路路 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會跑出版的路線 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	難以預測 , 在未來的情況下 , 很難做預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車上 , 車輛和摩托車 , 有85英哩之外 , 我知道你有這樣的經驗 , 說: 「 沒錯 ! 85英哩 ! 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上走路大概是大約一半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看到他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英里 , 他在地圖上看到那個傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他在地地地圖上 , 估計他會持續85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你知道 , 因為他耳朵會知道 , 因為他耳朵會在耳朵中看到 , 因為他耳朵會說: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘、摩托車、摩托車 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出理由預測車輛的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是新生素 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	那麼 , 我們要如何做到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從一個簡單的數據開始 , 分享我們的車輛 , 分享我們的車輛 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我在我的車子裡 , 我有一個非常精準的點子 , 我有非常精準的思考 , 我有非常精準的點子 , 和相機在我的車子裡 , 我有一個非常精準的點子 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	電腦視覺時 , 我估算在哪裡 , 他們會在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他汽車一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以擁有一個精準的概念 , 和其他車輛的概念一樣 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車輛分享這些數據 , 他們會怎麼做呢 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	電腦模擬器和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 並且在電腦模擬中發現 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也用了微小的溝通器官溝通 , 機器人和彼此溝通 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此互相互相時 , 它們會互相溝通 , 它們可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們處理了一些問題 , 我們會遇到一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 你要處理所有包裝 , 所以你要處理所有包裝 , 所以你要處理這些問題 , 才能幫助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車輛都追蹤預測軌道 , 你不需要注意到這些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個人看起來看起來有點不好 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會離開 , 你知道如何 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道駕駛的駕駛方式是你需要的 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要做我們最好的方法是誰 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車輛會說: 「 你需要從哪裡來 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	它依賴兩件事:一個 , 車輛的駕駛機率 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或你知道 , 做些什麼 , 他們並不可能在急診室裡做些什麼 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一系列的研究模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 我們可以偵測一下 , 如果駕駛機可以偵測到 , 我們可以偵測到如果駕駛器在手機上 , 或有一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測 , 誰 , 車輛是最好的位置 , 來計算安全的路徑 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術已經存在了 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為最大的問題是我們自己願意分享我們的數據 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個很不可思議的車輛 , 我們會在車輛上走路 , 我們會在車上走路 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以做到 , 以保護隱私的方式 , 就像現在 , 當我在看你的車外的時候 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我去看你的清單 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車可以在我們背後背後 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是個很棒的事情 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你在你面前的青少年 , 如果你真的不希望你能注意到你在你面前的青少年 , 你就來了 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由分享我們的數據 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 咱們來談一下你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓路更安全 。

medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療衛生博林skysky3分鐘 , 估計顯示在一個細胞內部長的生命 。

david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinskyimdbolinsky 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學師 , 我從一個非常不同的觀點來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 我一直在研究 , 因為我長大 , 表達真實和美麗的藝術和美麗 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很美妙的事情 , 因為他們對他們的真相和美好事物 , 都是很美好的 , 因為他們對他們有很美好的事物 , 像是理想的理想 , 可以被科學和美好的理想結合在一起 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達是關於真相的真相 , 意思是 , 他們是你能崇拜的 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	他們是很有力的 , 它們是很有力的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨特的 , 通常很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以拍攝影像 , 因為我不想看看我的螢幕 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美好的事情通常是常常常常常常常常常常常常發生在科學中 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是描述真實和美麗的詞彙 , 通常只能讓你了解語言和美麗的事物 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你仔細觀察宇宙的宇宙 , 你看到的宇宙是非常難以理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	然後我被教導 , 被教導師 , 我的視覺指導師 , 我想要找出一個方法來幫助人們了解真相和美麗的生物科學 , 用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相 , 和視覺的證據 , 來幫助人們了解真相 , 和視覺的證據 , 來幫助人們了解真相 , 和視覺的證據 , 來幫助大家了解真相 , 和視覺的證據 , 來幫助大家了解真相 , 和美麗的生物科學 , 來幫助人們了解真相 , 和視覺的證據 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	學生們常常在環境中被教導 , 但他們學到的是 , 他們學到的事物是相反的 , 但他們學到的是被教導的 , 但他們學到的不是總是證據 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像那個古老的古老餅乾 , 把雞湯帶進香味 , 直到你喝雞雞湯 。

and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛大學在哈佛大學 , 幾年前 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊和我有興趣 , 他會問我 , 如果我的團隊 , 我很有興趣 , 希望我能夠改變醫學和細胞生物學院 。 他問我 , 如果我的團隊 , 我很有興趣 , 希望我能夠改變醫學和細胞生物學院 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始探索一個專案 , 來探索真相和細胞的生物學 , 讓學生可以理解更大的圖片 , 來探索這些事實的真相 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	牠們可以擁有一個大型、複雜的城市 , 大型、複雜的城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微小的心臟是生命的心臟

so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們把這些分子聚在一起 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們用了這些資訊 , 它們是從細胞內部長到的細胞 , 它們會看到和感知 , 它們會從細胞內部流動 , 它們會看到和感知 。

but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器互相交互作用 , 它們真的很神奇 , 它們真的是非常神奇的 , 因為這些機器互相互相作用 。

this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 「 kinesin 」 , 它需要在細胞內製造出一種東西 , 或修復它 。
