and so what does that look like ? typical .	這看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙裡的典型的樣子是怎麼樣的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在非常高解析度的空間中 , ted有了高解析度的解析度 , 透過空間的觀點來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	我們能看到它嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不行 , 不論是完全黑暗的 , 完全黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	非常黑暗 , 如果你要去看近恆星的恆星 , 你仍然不會看到它的光線 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙是多麼大 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管如此亮亮 , 很聰明 , 如此亮亮 , 很明顯的 , 它會殺死你在幾光年內的夜晚 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 遠遠遠離你看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	它也非常寒冷 , 超過三度 , 絕對零 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它很空氣 , 很空氣 , 空氣是從這個地方的最佳的技術 , 來源於這個地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	通常是這樣 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	我們有燈光嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何知道環境的環境很遙遠 , 遠遠遠遠 , 遠遠遠遠 , 外星 , 和外星人相處 。
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球我們的環境 , 我們環境的形式是創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這意味著什麼 ? 遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠遠超過我們剛剛所說的 , 看起來像是星星 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 平等 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	意思是 , 看起來像是恆星 , 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們在幾十億年前 , 數十億年前 , 銀河系的黑洞 , 形成了一個巨大的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 引力爆發的能量引力爆炸 , 引力爆炸的能量 , 引力爆炸的能量 , 引力爆炸 , 引力爆炸 , 引力爆炸 , 引力爆炸 , 引力崩潰 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理是不太可能的 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法生存下來 , 來描述它發生在哪裡 , 像是在那段時間中 , 來描述它的樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	它會有點像是超級新星爆炸 , 但在幾百萬年的時間內 ,
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 幾十億年後 , 在宇宙中 , 有些化學物質可以準確地預測 , 並且解釋 , 在宇宙中 , 有些化學物質可以正確地描述它 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且解釋 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個身體系統 , 大腦 , 包含了一種精確的模型 , 大腦 , 包含了它的運作模式 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是一個超級的圖像 , 它也包含了相同的數學關係和相同的數學關係和相同的關係 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識的知識 。 如果那不夠奇怪 , 信仰是知識的知識 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	物理學的特性是特定的 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這樣的身體物體 , 不相同的數學和理念 , 不管它們可能是不可能的 , 同時也不限於它 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是化學分裂的化學物質 , 這種化學物質是不同的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構和原始的結構 , 不管是物理世界的結構 , 不管其他地方 , 甚至是物理世界的結構 , 而不是其他地方 , 它的確是物理世界的結構 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 我們如何與其他宇宙的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	關於史蒂芬•霍金斯的特定物理學 , 沒有特別的意見 , 但它是真實的 , 但它是真實的 , 但它是真實的 , 但它是真實的 , 但它是真實的 , 但它是真實的 , 沒有特殊的物理 , 沒有特殊的物理 , 沒有特殊的物理 , 沒有特別的意見 , 和任何特殊的物理 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中之一是 , 電腦的知識是資訊處理的過程 , 電腦並不需要電腦 , 不需要電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 更重要的是 , 我們也需要能量 , 才能讓媒體影響到我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 更小的 , 不應該是證據 , 但基本上就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境受到證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們會在300年前 , 來測試 , 說 , 新頓的法律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是證據顯示我們在地球上每平方公平方米的數十億年都一直在前進 , 還會持續數十億年 , 並且繼續下降 , 接下來的數十億年 , 還會持續下降 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就如我們所知 , 證據證明 , 證據證明地球上最基本的真相 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置是充滿證據和能量的
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在國際空間中 , 那些三個偏遠的空間 , 最低的可能供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如同我說的 , 它很冷 , 它很冷 , 很冷 , 不是嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另一個公園的錯誤概念 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一下 , 宇宙的空間 , 和我們的家一樣大小 , 現在 , 太陽系很空 , 但它仍然意味著它包含了數百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬個國家的確有一百萬個公開的公共衛生 , 說 , 一個自閉的空間站 , 在那裡 , 有一百萬個公開的公開的知識 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 它是超越了科技 , 將其它元素放入其他元素中 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 宇宙是 , 如果有些東西不是被法律物理的宇宙 , 那麼 , 若我們無法避免我們 , 那麼 , 可能是如何防止我們去做它呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識的知識 , 不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能做到 , 我們會是核融合反應器和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再次 , 看起來 , 人類的角度看不見 , 但所有人都要用望遠鏡 , 去看 , 看看你會看到相同的銀河 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更大的望遠鏡 , 你會看到恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些銀河系中 , 你會可以做天體物理學法 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	基本粒子的粒子物理和化學 , 等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	或許最困難的科學是生物學領域 , 因為它會花幾億年的時間 , 來到地球上最難的行星 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 我想我們只能用幾億年來做些什麼 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 在宇宙中 , 任何生物都可以變成類似的知識 , 如同我們在宇宙中所知的知識 , 不管我們是如何存在的 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	我們不是在一個獨特的時刻 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果國際空間可以創造出一個開放式的空間 , 基本上就是地球 。 所以 , 地球是地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制工廠 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很有限 , 因為它們很有限 , 但知識是很大的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種宇宙的知識也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 若沒有特定的知識 , 才能讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 我們不會生存下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	一切都死於超級新星 , 然後我們就死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們的脆弱性武器 , 從天體到科學實驗 , 大規模毀滅 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明已經只有50%的機會 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在場會談談這件事 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為這問題是正確的 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但是我同意他 , 我們能活下來 , 我們能活下來 , 我們能活下來 , 我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它依賴於機會 , 但它依賴於機會 , 但它依賴於機會 , 但它依賴於機會 , 但它依賴於機會 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是在所有物種滅絕的物種滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明 , 所有物種和文明已經存在歷史上 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	若我們希望能創造出新的解釋 , 我們的特殊關係 , 我們的特殊關係 , 我們的特殊關係 , 我們的特殊關係 , 我們的能力創造出新的解釋 , 我們的特殊關係 , 我們的特殊關係 , 是我們的能力 , 創造出新知識 , 來創造出新知識 。

and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 但不是正確的物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 我是物理學家 , 不論是物理學家 , 不論是物理學家 , 不論是物理學家 , 不論是物理學家 , 不論是物理學家 , 不論是物理學家 , 不論是物理學家 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果這是真的 , 我們最好的選擇就是預防二氧化碳排放在經濟活動上 , 以上數百億美元或任何理所當然 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它的行為 , 可能已經太遲了 , 也可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 也可能已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代末期 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 在1970年代末期 , 科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放量 , 可能已經太遲了 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	對於我來說 , 我不知道為什麼它不公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們不只知道 , 我們總是知道 , 如何解決它的成本 , 不然 , 我們總是知道 , 若我們不清楚 , 就會知道 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防 , 不可避免的問題 , 我們無法預測的原則 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的問題 , 而不是只是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	真的 , 這種預防的預防 , 只是如果我們知道要防止什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你一直在鼻子上 , 醫學的科學不是教導你如何避免爆發 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學停止尋找治療方法 , 結果就會達成很少 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界在氣體排放大量減少氣體排放量 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	為了減少溫度的溫度 , 並且鼓勵氣候變遷 , 讓陽光降低溫度 , 更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率、更有效率 。

and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	而我們沒有意識到的能力 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 , 而是生存的能力 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩隻石頭 , 把兩顆石頭放在它們上 。

how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個經濟學家保羅•羅倫•羅倫理想: 「 克里斯•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫•羅倫斯 」 說: 「 克里斯•羅倫 」 的意思是: 「 克萊特城市 」 , 「 公共衛生 」 的政策 , 如果它被關聯的國家分離貧窮 。

it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它對我們來說是個非常令人驚奇的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做他們的家庭作業 , 因為他們沒有任何電力 。

so here is the puzzle .	這是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼它會用科技來製造電池 , 但不需要用一百年的科技來製造電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以防止它可以預防的新技術 , 讓人們能用新科技 , 讓它們可以預防 , 像nelson一樣 。
what kinds of rules ?	規則是什麼 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	在這個國家的公司中 , 每單單位的電廠都要賣掉 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 不管是資源 , 其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他可以看到 , 規則規則規則規則規則規則規則規則 , 所以他們有了更多的客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	手機公司的規則是nelsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchsonpurchson
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統也看過這些規則如何運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試圖改變規則 , 讓它可以改變規則 , 但從商業和消費者身上 , 他們想要保存存活率的範圍 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以 , 他被困在法規上 , 協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson在街燈上進行研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試圖找出我們要如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們有一些規則來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 如果我們能選擇更多的選擇 , 或更多的選擇 , 就能做出實際的選擇 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的相互相互相反 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你想要給予領導者的選擇 , 選舉一個選擇的選項 , 選擇你可能會想要給予領導者的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們想要選擇可以持續消耗能源電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你給你一個方塊 , 你就會有壓力或摩擦 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法 , 來改變規則 , 使我們陷入困境 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , nelson也能取得網路 。

but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 更深層的了解、文化、文化、價值、信仰、文化、價值和信仰 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們會做出選擇 , 他們做出選擇 , 造成了非常多樣性的道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變我們使用與彼此互動的規則 , 更好 , 更好 , 更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。

what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地的規則是壞的 , 因為政府是壞的 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不是因為政府太強大和壓縮 , 因為政府太強烈和壓縮 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造環境的環境 , 我們不只會這樣 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們必須找到方法來建立 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大規模地表達出潛力和規則的挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這張圖中 , 中國是世界上的高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國的科技像是風格、印刷、印刷、印刷機 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從未被鼓舞 , 至少在那段期間 , 最有效的規則 , 可以鼓勵廣泛的傳播 。

so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	其他國家都在發展新科技 , 但也開發出新的技術 , 同時開發新型態 , 同時開發出新的規則 , 並且開發出新的規則 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入的收入 , 讓它在世界各地出現 。

growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的中國開始快速地成長 。

the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最聰明的地點 , 你可以看到在網路上 , 這是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是20世紀的中國 , 大部分的中國都在中國 , 大部分二十世紀 , 由英國的規則 , 都被英國人所禁止 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 在1950年代 , 香港是數百萬人可以從馬地開始工作 , 像是衣服、玩具 。

hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也就是 「 香港 」 的模式 , 當他們決定把整個馬地轉移到市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 密切的重要性 , 對於他人的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 不管在哪裡 , 都可以做些特別的國家 , 讓機會和市場規劃 , 讓機會和市場規範 , 讓機會與市場規則 , 讓機會與市場規範合作 , 讓機會與市場規範合作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們創造了四個特殊的經濟區塊 , 城市長大 , 很快速地 , 在那裡 , 城市長大 , 很快地 , 在那裡 , 城市長大 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	其中一座城市叫艾倫•蓋茲 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在城市中 , 有一座城市的工程碑 , 讓iphone有許多人 , 他們用了工程 , 讓iphone從中國搬到海岸 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	在這四個特殊區塊 , 牠們有14個特區 , 在那裡 , 牠們會被開放 , 最終證明了 , 牠們會被捕捉到的原因 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展示了成功的結果 , 讓整個經濟的市場模式融合起來 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示我們有幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一是:保存選擇的人 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的情況下 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你能做到這一點 , 但村莊可能是很小的 , 但村子會很少 , 可以做到這一點 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變規則的規則 , 你不能給一些人機會 , 來看看它的規則 , 並且嘗試改變規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會創造出新的規則 , 讓人們能選擇的機會 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們大大足夠大量 , 才能得到所有利益 , 才能得到所有利益 , 才能得到所有利益的利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 建議是我們稱作 「 公共衛星市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一座公開的規律開始 , 規則需要吸引我們的人 , 才能吸引我們城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者的投資者 , 來創造出基礎建設的投資者 , 建造出基礎設施的投資者 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引人 , 才能僱用那些人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 讓孩子們接受教育 , 讓孩子們接受教育 , 讓孩子們接受教育 , 讓孩子們接受教育 , 來幫助他們 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這條路 , 人們會移動 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以把這個模型放大 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以再次重複它 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它運作 , 我們需要良好的規則 , 我們已經討論了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些被捕捉到 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	若我們能建立城市的可能性 , 就能建立城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未知覺的地點開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新檔案中 , 但沒有人能活下來 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是選擇領導者 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們希望領導者的需求 , 我們想要領導人合作 , 來合作 , 來合作 , 來建立 , 來到中國和英國一起合作 , 去建立 , 來到中國和英國一起合作 , 來到中國和英國一起合作 , 來到中國和英國一起合作 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種程度上來說 , 英國 , 不可思議的行動 , 比所有援助計畫 , 更能減少世界貧窮 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們能讓這些夥伴可以把這些夥伴轉化 , 我們就能得到這些益處在世界各地 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些案例中 , 政府負責任意的責任任意 , 負責任意的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 。 但重要的是 , 了解到我們開始思考這些東西 , 可以讓我們開始思考這些東西 , 可以把我們的能力帶回來 , 可以把我們的能力帶回去探索新的想法 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不像殖民主義呢 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	關於殖民主義 , 最糟的是 , 在我們援助計畫中 , 它是關於殖民主義 , 而在我們援助計畫中 , 事情是很糟的 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這種模式是選擇 , 和那些在這些新地方的人們一起生活 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是 , 選擇是反對和自閉症的 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在練習上 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	咱們來做一個特定的領導者 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	他有機會去做中國 , 但他沒有一個香港 , 中國 , 但他沒有一個香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 在南邊有一個非常特別的位置 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	有一塊土地 , 一塊土地 , 一塊塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯特在加拿大說: 「 看 , 阿拉達和說法是很糟糕的 。
they want to get out .	他們想要離開 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼不加拿大 , 加拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特定的特定區域 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市來建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人來到這裡 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	咱們帶著一個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的公民會搬到城市中 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會連結現代經濟和現代經濟和現代的經濟和現代世界 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 其他可能的模型會被試試嗎 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和領導人在非洲 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人都可以接受一個特殊的區塊 , 讓他們可以成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這是改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種方法來創造新規則 , 讓人們無關心 , 反而是創造出新的規則 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也知道 , 在某些方面 , 若他們能做出更多的信任 , 就能讓更多的信仰 , 可以讓更多的信仰貸款 , 來建立道路 , 讓更多的信仰可以讓更多的信仰 , 可以讓更多的信仰 , 來建立道路 , 讓更多的信仰 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	或許甚至有點像是 「 人工智慧帳戶 」 , 你把土地放在帳戶旁邊 , 把土地放在帳戶旁邊 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	在非洲 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸拍攝的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的土地 , 有數十萬人可以活下來 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個概念放到城市中 , 數十億個城市 , 不僅僅是有足夠的城市 , 可以幫助創造數十億個城市 , 來到城市中有足夠的城市 。
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在世界各地 , 如果我們觀察光燈在晚上 , 它看起來就像大多數世界都已經建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我來說明為什麼這是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有土地 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它轉化成一個平方 , 把它放在地球上 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表土地 , 讓這些點代表土地 , 已經在城市三十億人居住了 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些植物放到你所看到的城市中 , 只有三十億個城市居住的城市居住居住了三十億城市居住的城市 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要建立城市十億人 , 他們就會這樣做 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從3%到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅地減少人類腳印在地球上 , 讓人們可以移動 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是城市 , 人們有機會能取得工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到基本的電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造出第一座城市 , 我們建造了更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助有人性 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可以寫一些細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不想讓我們走出城市 , 去設計他們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學術在野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以想像一下問題 , 假設它不僅僅是加拿大 , 而是加拿大 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西是加入的參與者 , 可能是巴西 , 或許巴西 , 可能是巴西的參與者 , 或巴西 , 可能是巴西的參與者 , 可能是巴西的參與者 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫作治療 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒那麼多 , 但它可以輕易運作 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何融入這個呢 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 木頭和香港是城市 , 牠們有一大堆積木 , 牠們在牠們自己開始的時候 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用在土地上的價值 , 讓它變得更有價值 , 但學校系統和健康照護系統和健康照護系統 , 更有價值的人 , 讓它變得更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	因此 , 人們協助建構這個區塊 , 建立基礎規則 , 並建立這個區塊 , 並建立基礎規則 , 讓它變得非常正確 。
so there are many other details like this .	還有許多其他細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們應該要做些什麼 , 讓這些建築能有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 因為它們是安全的 , 所以他們不會降低成本 , 或颶風 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多科技細節已經開始追求這些事情 , 但我們已經開始追求這些東西 , 不只能說 , 沒有道路 , 沒有阻礙 , 沒有阻礙 , 沒有阻礙 , 不管我們在哪裡 , 還能讓我們走出一個真正的全球性力 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我結合這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們的原因是 , 儘管有許多人在地球上 , 是因為它的理念 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以與別人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像恐怖的物品 , 鯊魚代表我們彼此變得更少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們就會變得更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們想到科技時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則的規則 , 像是我們如何與彼此溝通 , 例如 , 我們的規則 , 可以提供一些知識自由的知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	我們有一個系統 , 在政府辦公室裡 , 人們可以帶領土地 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們可以繼續進步 , 我們的規則會改變規則 , 我們不得不用規則來改變規則 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 所以 , 人們喜歡nelson和他的朋友不需要在街燈上走路 , 才能繼續進步 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組的基因團隊已經發現了 , 遠遠地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地地圖 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna和海岸 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	在這場辯論中 , 我被問過幾位關於 「 辯論 」 的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者很喜歡 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	接下來我要告訴各位 , 在我18分鐘內 , 我們要從閱讀基因編碼開始寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅僅僅十年前 , 我們出版了第一條序列 , 即使我們出版出版的第一條序列 , 即便是 「 無人機體 」 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫從13年來 , 只花了三年的時間 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內進行同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年間 , 許多基因組成了人類的基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在這個階段的基因組中 , 我們大概有三到五個基因組序列 , 大概有三到五個基因組 , 大概有三到五個基因組 , 大概有三到五個基因組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們只是從環境機體的一方案例中找到了130個基因組 , 結果是 , 未來的130個基因組 , 正是從環境機體中找到的 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	閱讀基因編碼已經改變了
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們發現 , 我們在這個星球上看到了什麼樣子 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人都不了解它 , 因為它們是不可見的 , 但微生物的生物大量超過一半 , 因為它們是可見的 , 但微生物的生物大量只有三分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	或許它是人類在牛津大學的一百萬個細菌 , 不管怎麼做 , 你就會發現 , 每一千萬個細菌 , 大約有一百萬個細菌 , 大約有一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	少於兩年前 , 我們決定要做些什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們就開始了 , 很棒的海洋地圖 , 試圖把海洋分析的數量 , 以三百英里的速度 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們在美國東岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 到海岸 , 到海岸 , 來到海岸 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的 , 因為我們正在做這個計畫 , 讓年輕人進入科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們把牠們的dna放進我們的實驗室裡 , 把牠們的dna帶到我們的實驗室裡 , 把牠們的dna回到我們的實驗室裡 , 把牠們的dna帶到我們的實驗室裡 , 把牠們的dna回到我們的實驗室裡 , 把牠們的dna帶到我們的實驗室裡 , 把牠們的dna帶到我們的實驗室裡 , 把牠們的dna回到我們的實驗室裡 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	這樣做 , 我們做了一些令人驚發現的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 我們眼睛的眼睛只有一個或兩種機體 , 牠們在環境中有相同的偏見 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎每個物種在海洋中 , 牠們的能量和溝通方式是一樣的 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個網站上 , 我們發現了1.3萬個新物種 , 我們發現了1.3百萬個新的基因 , 及超過五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	現在我們已經把這台空氣從土地基金融合起來 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們要測量多少種病毒和細菌 , 特別是在飛機或關閉的病毒 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們收集了一些簡單的應用程式 , 我們收集了十億個微生物 , 來自於紐約市的一座建築 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們在這個過程中 , 正在進行的過程 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在海洋中 , 我們發現幾乎每百英哩 , 我們在海洋中看到極多樣性的樣本 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些邏輯的邏輯 , 以不同的溫度分裂 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 我們發現在溫暖的溫度下降低溫度 , 溫暖和冷水的差異 , 看起來很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一件令人驚訝的是這些感測器偵測了不同波長的光線 , 我們可以預測 , 在它們的光線上 , 我們能預測它們的光線 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些是從區域到區域的區域 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不令人驚訝 , 在深海中 , 大部分藍色光是藍色光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有許多綠色的光線時 , 他們看到很多綠色光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但他們更有可能在極端的情況下發射光線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了嘗試找出我們的基因數據 , 包括我們所有的資料包含所有資料 , 包括我們的基因數據 , 包括地球上所有資料包含了超過29萬個基因資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試圖把這些發現新成員的新成員 , 我們發現新成員 , 或我們發現了新的家庭 。
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每個新的家庭中 , 我們有五萬個主要的基因家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們在這個星球上最早發現的基本基因組和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著 「 演化樹 」 時 , 我們就在右邊和動物之間 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約有2萬5千萬個基因 , 我們只有大約2萬5千萬個基因 , 我們只有在我們的基因中 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物聚在一起 , 我們大概會有三萬個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我看這些基因不僅僅是演化的設計
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在基因組合中 , 基因組合的樣子是基因組合的樣子 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , dna已經改變了dna的能力 , 在過去十年或兩年間 , dna的速度非常快速 , 非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組的基因組 , 從1995年到1995年 , 基因組成基因組成分 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 說: 「 我心靈感 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約是500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	hemophilus有180個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 比較小的基因 , 可能是比較小的組合 , 會如何 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做交響樂器 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯器是基因編碼的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們在基因內分裂 , 它們就會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一個地圖 , 把所有基因組合起來 , 我們稱之為 「 非性基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現環境非常重要 , 因為環境的重要性是非常關鍵的 , 你只能定義一個基本上或非基因基礎 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智慧方法來觀察它們在共通點之間的相互作用 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們發現 , 只有173個基因組合在一起 , 我們發現只有173個基因 , 共有三個基因 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	若我們忽略了一顆紅外線 , 它擴散了更多 , 如果我們忽略了一顆紅外線 , 它擴散到三十多次 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	因此我們認為我們可以擴展或吸引基因組 , 以大約300到400個基因組 , 從最低到500個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法是建立一個人工染色體 , 而我們必須在其中一個人工染色體 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現合成的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	漢密斯密和我同事 , 開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 使我們能夠合成5000個鹼基的同事 , 一種令人興奮的新方法 , 使我們能夠合成一百分之百的生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一種非常令人興奮的實驗 , 我們把合成的dna結合成dna , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒的第一次合成病毒 , 它只花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是一張卡通的卡通 , 184年的卡通 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是軟體的軟體 , 我們有生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們會立刻去評估這個區域 , 特別是委員會員 , 我在一個委員會立刻 , 去評估這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為它很重要的是要保持真實的想像力 , 和人們的想像力 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 基本上 , 任何病毒都是基因組所組成的 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上想到伊波拉或小波拉的dna , 但dna並不是感染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以 , 即使有人製造了基因組 , 那dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的關注是設計師 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和蘇聯的國家 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 主要努力試圖創造出生物的戰場 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這研究真的很少 , 就應該有很少的活動 , 來做設計師在未來的情況 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞有機體可能是兩年 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	或許在十年內 , 我們已經有了可能性 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	現在我們有了數十個不同的建構 , 因為我們可以把蛋白質和基因放進這個人工染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你如何把所有其他人物放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有了一種重大的組合體制 , 將這些碎片帶到染色體上 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個機體的機制 , 可以用三百萬種輻射而非被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它的基因組在204小時內放射到24小時後 , 牠的基因組在這個輻射後被解放出來 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種機體在地球上有機體 , 而且存在於地球上 , 可能現在在地球上 , 存在於我們的旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是玻璃的玻璃片 , 大約是5000萬次輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始被燒掉 , 而微生物在底部的微生物變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張照片 , 結果是:這張圖表顯示出了7百萬個輻射的結果 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體是完全的染色體 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	相同的dna自動化合約24小時 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	非常令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千個不同的物種 , 這些生物可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組中 , 第一個步驟是將它們移植到細胞沒有基因組 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此 , 我們認為合成細胞會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅能了解生物學的基礎 , 以及社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 二氧化碳來自環境中 , 二氧化碳來自環境中 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的機體 , 有數以千計的生物 , 可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	因此 , 我們從大氣中使用碳 , 把碳從大氣中使用碳 , 將它們從大氣中轉換成過程 , 用碳和捕捉它的碳 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一氧化碳分子 , 我們用它來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	同時 , 有許多路徑 , 可能是工程碑的路徑 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜普森林的大型計畫 , 用在挪威 , 來捕捉並將甲烷從氣體變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短期內 , 我認為 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來製造一個新型的基因組合法 , 我們認為我們能設計一個機器人 , 來製造一個新型的基因組合成千萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	所以 , 隨著生物學 , 你只能觀察到氫生產、化學生產、化學產品 , 或可靠 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的角色是如何 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試圖修復原理 , 來製造氫氣直接從太陽光合作 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞的酵素 , 酵素會分裂成簡單糖和酵素的酵素 , 酵素會分裂成簡單糖和酵素 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥品已經在主要實驗室使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中化學的化學成分 , 比我們最好的化學家能生產 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程可以是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 , 希望能成為食物的源源 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我和政策研究有關 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們從1999年開始在1999年開始進行實驗 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物思維 , 直到我們去做一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教參與 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這真的是個非常奇怪的研究 , 因為有許多宗教領袖們都在做這些實驗 , 因為他們沒有辦法找到任何東西 , 只能給我們去做這些實驗 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會在這個領域中 , 我們試圖建立好的例子 , 來研究這個領域 , 並且我們在這個領域的研究 , 來研究這個領域 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	對於生物恐怖分子而言 , 它們是非常簡單的問題 , 因為它們是非常簡單的 , 我們不只能用各種簡單的問題 , 來製造乾淨能源 , 或許能改革開發中國家能提供各種簡單的問題 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家哲學家菲利浦•薩維•薩維•辛巴帕說過:我們人生中最初步的步驟 , 來改善我們的人生 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、心理學、心理學、心理學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利浦•薩維比薩維比薩維•辛巴帕有所謂的健康 。

philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦•薩姆貝蒂:讓我們在亞當達的教堂中談到這段話題 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 ! 」 「 來吧 。 」 「 我做 。 」 「 我做 。 」

i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想麻煩 。 」

life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是反射性的 , 反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	早期的熱情就會降低 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年的青少年 , 愛滋病和婚姻謝謝你喬治 , 親愛的青少年 , 每年有60% , 愛滋病 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都沒有使用生氣控制 。
so much for promises .	為了承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在 , 咱們來試試四歲的孩子 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	牠們可以有兩隻 。 但如果他們等到實驗器回來 , 他們就可以有兩隻 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	孩子們有三分之二的孩子 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不等等待 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抵抗神殿 , 以後的誘惑 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	我的同事在史丹佛大學畢業後 , 我同事在史丹佛大學回14年後 , 試圖發現那些孩子的同事 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 孩子們有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	孩子們拒絕了250個高度 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很龐大 , 像是一整組不同的iq點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有麻煩 , 更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們有自信和決心的關鍵 , 我今天的關鍵是 , 你的關鍵是 , 他們的關鍵是 , 對你來說 , 它們是未來的 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	今天我要談的是什麽 ?
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間分析是人類經驗的研究 , 分析你人類體驗到時間分裂或時間的分裂 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動化和非意識 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化之間之間 , 彼此之間之間之間的關係 , 在社會課間之間 , 彼此之間之間之間的關係 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們會變得偏見 , 因為你學會會變得偏見 , 因為你學會會變得偏見 。
what determines any decision you make ?	決定你做出什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做了一個決定 , 你要做一個決定 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 你的感覺是甚麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 他們會稱之為 「 開放 」 , 因為他們的焦點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 重點是不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	一直在過去的情況是: 「 我經歷過什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策是基於過去記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱之為 「 過去 」 , 因為他們關注在哪裡 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 不是現在 , 而是未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點都是關於預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們會稱他們為 「 未來 」 , 他們聚焦在未來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間矛盾 , 我想要爭論 , 每一決策你都沒意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	名字是 , 你有這種偏見的程度 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有兩種方法 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式是未來的 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在過去 , 或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以稱之為 「 專注於生命 」 或 「 專注於生命 」 的喜悅 , 不管你是如何控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以成為未來的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者你可以是 「 生命 」 , 生命開始在死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出靈活的需求 , 使你必須學習去做這件事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快的 , 最佳的時間是如何 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高速的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於過去負面和自由主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最樂觀的結合是你從過去的親戚身上得到的結果 , 你將你的家人、身分和你的家人、身分和你的家人 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來的新挑戰 , 來到新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在所做的是能量 , 來探索自己、人類、空間、空間 , 來探索自己 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間都比正面的更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來的犧牲是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲了家庭的時間 , 他們犧牲了家人 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了好玩 , 他們犧牲了個人的成本 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了睡眠 , 所以它會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們生活在工作、成果和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我肯定會和一些tedsterstersterstersterstersterstersters 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是南布朗克斯•墨西哥的小小孩子 , 在南布朗克斯•蓋爾 , 一個小小的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯•蓋爾 , 在南布朗克斯區的一家人住 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我在這裡是一位未來的成員 , 那些犧牲了 , 因為老師們介入了我 , 讓我成為未來的機會 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不吃 , 直到我學到平衡 , 直到我學到平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了專注於過去的比例 , 比我更有生產力 , 更有價值 , 比我更有價值 , 我也比過去更有生產力 , 我更高興 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說我們正在應用在許多世界問題:改變我們在學校的孩子們 , 解決方案 , 和保育 , 改善醫療照護 , 和保育 , 改善的成癮 , 和保育 , 和保育計畫 , 改善了數量的經濟學童 , 和保育 , 改善人心 , 和保育 , 改善了數十億人的死亡率 , 和保育 , 和保育 , 改善了美國的經濟學童 , 和保育 , 和保育 , 預期 , 更有50% 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說:許多生命的謎題可以解決 , 以理解你的觀點和其他人 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 但我認為後果是很簡單的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	幾百年來 , 2010年 , ted2010年 , ted2010年的《長期新聞》 , 《長期新聞》的報導 , 不僅僅是重要的 , 而是在我們未來的數目中 , 來追蹤我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球性的議題、媒體、新聞、科學 。

what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那麼呢 ? 我們要如何餵養九十億人呢 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在已經麻煩了六十億 。

what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界各地都很不一樣 , 如果中國設立了政府 , 就會變得非常不同 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	全球最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經開始做dna測試 , 讓他們開始做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職涯 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的限制 , 才能引導我們所知的限制 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	有些最近的發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 但南極洲 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 但南極洲 , 每塊大陸都已經擴大到大陸 , 但南極洲 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 而生命可能不再需要我們 , 而生命可能不再需要我們 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎沒有我們 , 生命會出現 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但是我在月球上發現月球的長新聞 。

nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	太空、科技、科學、太空、科技、宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳•帕羅斯我們來到土星 。

and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	地球上 , 地球上的所有地方 , 我們都開始尋找答案 , 來源於太空飛行 , 飛行星球 , 飛行星球飛行 , 到204年夏天 , 飛行星球飛行 , 太空船飛行 , 到204年夏天 , 飛行星球的飛行器 , 以至於2004年夏天 , 太空船飛行 , 以至於2004年夏天 , 以至於2004年夏天 , 太空船飛行的速度 , 直到2004年夏天 , 飛行星球飛行 , 直到2004年夏天 , 飛行星球飛行 , 直到2004年夏天 , 飛行星空飛行 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個豐富的行星系統 。

saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星是非常龐大且多樣化的 。

in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴西比亞•巴西比亞•巴西亞•巴西亞•巴西亞•巴西亞•巴西亞•布魯斯•布魯斯•布魯斯•布魯斯•布魯斯•布魯斯提出了一千萬個非暴力的抗爭者 , 來阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止障礙 , 來阻止阻止障礙 。

for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我一直在試圖終結結合和平行的作品 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 以色列與巴勒斯坦人說話 。

the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這問題時 , 我聽到這問題時 , 我聽到這問題時 , 通常我花了幾年的時間 , 用非暴力來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 來保護他們的土地和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正在嘗試 , 以非暴力運動來終結盟友 , 並在區域中建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人都可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這分裂在地面和平方的抗爭之處 , 是因為我們沒有人和平的抗爭 , 是因為我們沒有人和正義的抗爭者 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	今天我要來談談關於注意力的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 和你注意力的力量 , 在西岸和非暴力運動中 , 你的注意力是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 對於非暴力的非暴力 , 而是為了我們開始對抗非暴力的暴力 , 但對我們來說 , 對非暴力來說 , 那些已經有了不起的 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明這個村莊的村莊 , 叫做布魯斯 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕跡 , 因為伊斯蘭會在村莊裡建立一個公寓的區域 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 所以他們會失去了40%的土地 , 所以他們會失去他們的土地 , 所以他們會失去了40%的土地 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發性活動 , 他們開啟了一個和平的抗議活動 , 他們發起了一個和平的抗議活動 。
