julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞:當我第一次聽到關於布魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 國際媒體失敗了 , 在2003年 , 國際媒體失敗了 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	在十個月之後 , 阿拉伯和巴勒斯坦國際協調 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦的土地和巴勒斯坦人聯繫起來 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	巴勒斯坦的鄰居在耶路撒冷河岸邊走到巴勒斯坦街坊 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然很沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默的後果可以增長 , 甚至生存 , 甚至生存 , 或甚至生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力的抗爭和非暴力主義和非暴力的抗爭 , 他們都是一種共同點 , 他們都是一個共同點子的共同點 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	假如暴力的領導者 , 只能把國際關注放在巴勒斯坦問題上 , 難以避免受害者 , 使他們在巴勒斯坦議題上 , 使他們看到這些問題 , 會變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的注意力可能不會讓人驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓孩子長久以來 , 他注意到他的注意力 , 就是把他的注意力轉換給他注意 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	trum會成為童年心理學家稱之為功能行為 , 從孩子學到 , 孩子們就開始學習它 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以專注於他們的孩子 , 或缺乏行為的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為都可以影響 , 讓國際社區選擇聚焦點注意 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東和平 , 將非暴力領袖帶給我們改變非暴力的領導者 , 來改變非暴力的領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我的電影中 , 加薩和東部的影片 , 加薩和東部的影片 , 我看到了影響力的影響 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在村莊的村莊裡 , 社區和布德魯斯的村落非常相似 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去了許多土地 , 沒有自由 , 來到西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們花了兩年的時間 , 因為沒有人注意到 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個屏幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們告訴了最好的解答和分裂 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 在電影裡 , 人們會注意到 , 那些人在電影裡 , 看到他們在電影中看到的故事 , 那些人會說 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們不斷地繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	右邊是伊斯蘭教徒 , 它代表了 「 伊斯蘭教徒 」 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者是使用布達達成的主要招募工具 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導了非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的行動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華爾和蘇莉戲劇院的例子 , 可以扮演角色扮演角色扮演角色扮演角色扮演角色扮演角色扮演角色扮演角色扮演角色角色扮演角色扮演角色角色扮演角色 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家的力量 , 可以讓他們開始處理這些非暴力的暴力行為 , 像是布爾拉、珍珠、珍珠、珍珠、珍珠、珍珠、珍珠 , 和效果的影響力 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事就是要了解如果我們不把注意力放在這些努力上 , 它們是無法注意到的 , 它們是從來不會發生的 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我看過第一手 , 如果我們這麼做 , 它們就會多 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多麼 , 他們的影響就會成長在巴勒斯坦的衝突中 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響 , 終於無法阻止這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者證明 , 非暴力在像布德魯斯一樣 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意力 , 讓他們能證明它的工作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	史蒂芬•蓋爾•金恩是很簡單的 , 他的案例是: 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德、馬丁路德•金恩 , 還有他的例子 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	商業、企業、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	sinek:偉大的領導者啟發了行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你怎麼解釋當我們不認為我們假設時 , 會如何 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好 , 你如何解釋其他事情的結果 , 才能達成更好的事物 , 才能達成更好的事物 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果很創新呢 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 他們比所有的競爭更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有同樣的媒體 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁路德•金恩•金德王帶領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一的美國人 , 他肯定不是唯一的美國人 , 他也肯定不是唯一的男人 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何如此 , 權力控制權力的飛行器能控制控制權力、控制權力、控制權力的人 , 更好的 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有成員飛機 , 他們也沒有成員飛機 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我發現了
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深刻改變了我在思考世界的運作方式 , 甚至深深地改變了我的觀點 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有偉大、激勵的領導者和組織 , 不管是蘋果或馬丁•路德金 , 或馬丁•路德金 , 或馬丁•路德金 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這是完全相反的 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的是 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼一些組織和一些領導人 , 有些領導人也能啟發其他人 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我定義這個詞非常快
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個國家的每個組織 , 都知道他們有100% 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們如何做到它 , 不管你稱它為 「 你 」 或你的 「 你 」 或你的 「 你 」 或你的 「 交易 」 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道為什麼他們會這麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	為 「 為何 」 , 我不代表 「 創造利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 結果是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	由於 「 為什麼 」 我的意思是:你的目的是 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的信念是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上早上醒來 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們認為 , 我們的方式是從外面走進來的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 , 我們從最明顯的事物開始 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵領導者和鼓舞團體 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 都不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易了解 , 大家會這樣 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 市場訊息會像這樣的: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮設計 , 簡單地使用朋友 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一個嗎 ? 」 「 嗯 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這是大多數的銷售 , 大部分的人都在做 , 大部分的人都是這樣做 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們會說我們是怎樣的 , 我們會說我們是怎樣的 , 我們會說我們是怎樣的 , 我們會說我們是怎樣的 , 我們會這樣做 , 我們會說我們是怎樣的 , 我們會這樣做 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律:我們有最好的律師 , 是我們最好的律師 , 我們總是對我們的客戶做事 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的車輛:它有天空氣體 , 我們的車子 , 來買車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果的溝通方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們都相信在挑戰地圖上 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信在思考不同的情況下 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰的是把我們的產品設計出來 , 簡單地使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是要做好的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不對嗎 ? 你準備好要買電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的是反覆這些資訊 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	告訴我們 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們不買你做的事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 , 他們買你做的事 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋為什麼每個人在這個房間裡都很不舒服 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很適用蘋果的蘋果 , 或蘋果的蘋果 , 或蘋果的蘋果 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我所說的 , 蘋果只是電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼都沒有辦法讓他們從任何事業的競爭 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者是所有這些產品的競爭 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 幾年前 , 甘迺迪的電視劇烈 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很強大 , 讓平方的電視節目 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經製造了數年的螢幕
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	丹麥玩家和pds , 他們製造出很棒的品質產品 , 他們製造出很棒的產品 , 他們做出很棒的產品 , 他們做出完美的產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在我們甚至無法想像買三個玩家
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買一台電腦公司的公司 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 , 他們買你做的事 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標是不是要做任何事業的人 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要去做那些相信你相信的人 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	它都是在生物學中所做的 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看看人類腦袋 , 你看到的是 , 人類腦袋是從底部分裂出來的 , 你看到的是 , 人類腦袋裡的三種主要元素 , 和黃金圈一樣 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的腦部 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層對我們的理性和分析想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間有兩個功能 , 我們的大腦負責任意和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也對人類行為、決策 , 也沒有能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面上傳遞到外面時 , 人們可以了解大量的複雜資訊 , 像是特定、信息、信息、信息 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是不動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能控制行為時 , 我們會說 , 讓人們能控制行為 , 然後我們能控制行為 , 讓大家能控制行為 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是猜測的決定 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給別人所有事實和細節 , 說: 「 我知道 , 他們會說: 「 我知道這些事實和細節 , 只是沒有感覺 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這種詞彙 , 不是 「 感覺 」 。
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制語言的部分是控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的就是: 「 我不知道 , 沒錯 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	有時候你會說你是你的心臟 , 或者你是你的心靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭破壞你的行為 , 不是其他身體控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	大腦裡的所有事情都發生在你的腦袋裡 , 大腦控制決策和非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你這麼做 , 會如何讓人們回應你做的事 , 而人們回應為你做的事 , 而人們回應為你做什麼 , 或更重要的是 , 更重要的是 , 或更重要的是 , 要為你做些什麼 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再次 , 目標並不是只為了賣給那些你相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標並不是要僱用那些需要工作的人 , 而是僱用你相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你僱用人們 , 因為他們能做工作 , 如果你僱用你的錢 , 如果你僱用你的人 , 他們會工作 , 因為他們可以做工作 , 如果你僱用你的錢 , 你就知道 , 如果你僱用你的人 , 他們會用血液、汗和淚 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	另外還有更好的例子 , 比用更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在20世紀初期 , 人們飛行的趨勢就像是天空 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都嘗試它 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley , 我們假設是成功的 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 如果你問人們: 「 為什麼你的公司失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你同樣的相同的情況 , 第三件事情:受害、不好的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三件事 , 讓我們來探索 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpontlangley有五萬美金 , 讓五萬美金給了五萬美金 。
money was no problem .	錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在smithsmithsmithsoniansmithsmithsonian , 他知道所有偉大的心智 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的錢 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	《紐約時報》 , 每個人都在他周圍繞著他 , 每個人都在追蹤他 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠 , 在華盛頓天頓 , 沒有人我們認為是成功的成功 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們沒有錢 ; 他們沒有錢 ; 他們沒有錢 ; 他們沒有錢 ; 他們沒有錢 , 他們沒有錢 ; 他們沒有錢 , 他們還沒有錢 , 他們還沒有錢 , 還沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 給他們的夢想 , 給他們的夢想 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差異是 , 信念 , 信念 , 由一個目的 , 來源自自信 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出這台機器 , 它會改變世界的範圍 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要是富有的 , 他想要是富有的 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求財富 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	沒錯 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信 , 愛德華兄弟的夢想與他們有血液、汗和淚 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為了付錢 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 要花5個組件 , 因為那是多次 , 他們願意花5個組件 , 因為那是 , 他們願意花5個組件 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 直到1903年12月17日 , 沒有人能體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 拉ngley被誤解了 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 這是一個令人驚人的發現 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有錢 , 他沒有錢 , 他沒有錢 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 , 他們買你做的事 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信什麼 , 你就會吸引那些相信你相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信的人 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	關於創新的法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你肯定知道這個詞 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	第一2.5%的人是我們創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的員工 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期 , 你的主要和你的階段 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	唯一的原因是 , 因為你無法買電子手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都在各個地方都在這個數字上 , 因為如果你想要大量的預測 , 你就無法做到這點 , 因為如果你想要大量的預測 , 你就可以做到這點 , 直到達成目標的目標 , 到達成千分之三十八%的市場 , 直到達成目標 , 才能達到目標 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你在新商業上有什麼樣子 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你們: 「 喔 , 大約10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	你可以試試超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有10%的人只能得到它 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	像是那種感覺: 「 喔 , 他們只是得到它 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你在做事業時 , 要怎麼找到你在做事業的人 , 才會這樣做 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以它是這樣 , 因為 , 你看到的 , 早期的早期 , 早期的小小差不多 , 因為 , 你看到的 , 早期 , 早期就不會嘗試它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的員工 , 他們很舒服 , 來做那些猜測 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更努力做出那些直覺決策 , 那些直覺決策 , 就是他們所相信的世界 , 而不是只是產品 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這是他們第一次走進一家店的店裡 , 買一台手機 , 當他們第一次走進去買一台車時 , 每週都買了一台車 , 再來買iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些是花了四萬美金的電視 , 即使科技是最初期的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為科技是很棒的 , 他們也這麼做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一 。

how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你如何記得你在哪裡 ? 你如何記得你在哪裡 ? 你如何記得你在哪裡 ? 你知道嗎 ? 你如何記得你的車子 , 你記得你在哪裡 ? 神經學家的神經學家神經學家神經學家 , 神經學家的神經學家 , 神經學家的神經學家神經學家 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、科學、探索、神經科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilfges:你的大腦告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們公園停車時 , 我們會記得我們在公園裡停車嗎 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是問題的回家 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他腦袋裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們將從海馬迴的記憶體中開始 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有傷害 , 例如阿茲海默症 , 你無法記得東西包括你在阿茲海默症 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它在拉丁文的 「 海底 」 的名字 , 它是 「 海底 」 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	像其他大腦一樣 , 它是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類大腦大約有100億個神經元
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元互相溝通 , 互相溝通的神經元和彼此溝通 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	hpocampus是兩種細胞 , 它們非常密切連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解海洋的記憶如何運作 , 藉由記錄從個人神經元的神經元 , 或探索一個環境 , 來尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	我們會想像我們從一個神經元從一個神經元傳播到這裡 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發電時 , 就會有一個紅點和點子 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是 , 這種神經元知道 , 在它環境中 , 我們會看到一個特定的地方 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它的訊號會傳遞給大腦的訊號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以展示出神經元的功能 , 是動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元來觀察 , 我們會看到不同的神經元 , 我們會看到不同的神經元 , 像這個平方盒子一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們會形成一個地圖 , 與大腦聯繫在一起 , 說: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	細胞也記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要電力活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了電玩遊戲 , 他們在小鎮上移動 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	牠們在海裡的地點 , 就會開始發電流動 , 開始將電流動作 , 開始將電流動作 , 開始將電流動作 , 開始將電流傳送到鄉間 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個細胞的細胞知道哪裡是哪裡 , 或人在環境中 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的重要性 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 頂尖的頂尖像是在牆壁上升高的牆壁 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴大盒子時 , 就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	每一塊牆上 , 就會出現在南邊 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一塊牆放在盒子裡 , 就會把牆壁放在盒子裡 , 把其他牆壁放在盒子裡 , 把其他牆壁放在盒子裡 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 對於海馬迴路線的空間 , 對於海馬迴路線非常重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	實際上 , 細胞發現在海馬迴路上 , 細胞會發現這個計畫 , 來到海馬迴路線 , 到海馬迴路線 , 到海馬迴路線 , 到海馬迴路線 , 來到海馬迴路線 , 來到海馬迴路 , 來到海馬迴路 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的這個細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物在路線上移動時 , 就會看到 , 因為它是邊緣 , 或邊緣的細胞 , 在左邊的邊緣 , 或邊緣的邊緣 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 或邊緣的邊緣 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞 , 只要有兩座桌子 , 就會被丟掉 , 或牆壁或牆壁 , 或兩條桌子之間的關係 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是我們認為一個方法 , 就是我們認為細胞決定動物在哪裡 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體的樣子 , 像是這個目標 , 或在哪裡 , 你的車是哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看看它們的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放在環境中 , 通常他們會覺得旗子或車子是很好的 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變形狀和大小的形狀 , 像是我們和環境的形狀一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個例子中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗子如何改變形狀和環境的形狀 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方的環境中 , 你看到的是 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方的環境中 , 你看到的是 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方的環境中 , 你可以看到 , 如果旗幟是 , 他們認為旗幟是在一個小平方的環境中 , 而你在一個小平方的環境中 , 會讓環境更大 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	它就像你記得在哪裡的模式 , 然後你可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那位置位 , 然後你就可以回到那邊的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那邊的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這引導你回到你所想的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們正在經歷運動 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們走路路徑 , 可能公園 , 我們會停下來 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以在這個路上走路 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以在這個路上走路 , 以往往往往往 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	細胞的細胞也形成了這種路徑 , 稱為 「 網絡細胞 」 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	再次 , 神經細胞會發現 , 再次 , 它們就像細胞一樣 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但現在 , 每個個體的細胞 , 每個個體細胞都有不同的位置 , 每個個體的細胞 , 都在一個不同的位置 , 以一種非常不同的位置 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你用不同顏色的圖案 , 每個細胞都跟其他細胞的不同顏色相互相對 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的紅色則是這個紅色的紅色 , 上面的紅色 , 上面的紅色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 把它們的角度放在地圖上 , 用三角形的角度來看一下 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電力活動可以從一個細胞移動到下一個細胞 , 讓它可以用它來控制它的運作方式 , 讓它可以用它來控制它的運作 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有電池都有相同的對稱性 , 神經細胞之間的相同位置 , 它意味著 , 我們之間的神經元素 , 與其它之間的相互作用 , 它意味著 , 我們之間的神經細胞之間的相同位置 , 使我們在六個方向上移動 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人們放在mri掃描儀中 , 把他們放在mri掃描儀中 , 把他們放在mri掃描儀中 , 把他們放在mri掃描儀中 , 把他們放在mri掃描儀中 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	事實上 , 你可以看到它在人類的皮層中 , 你可以看到它在人類的皮層 , 大腦的一部分是大腦的一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他在車輛的距離 , 和他公園的距離 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這就代表了細胞的形狀細胞 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他從車公園的路徑走出車公園的路徑 , 它會代表在公園的路線上 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這類細胞可以製造出細胞的細胞 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	牠可以回到地位的位置 , 把牠帶到地位的位置 , 讓牠在大腦中最好的位置 , 把牠停下來的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個地點 , 像卡車一樣 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許它已經被淘汰了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道 , 他知道它是哪裡 , 所以他知道它在哪裡 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除此之外 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以它可能是神經機制 , 使我們想要想像它們 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶就可以開始 , 藉由細胞移動 , 來形成空間結構的空間結構 , 形成你周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以把這個觀點放在空間中 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 如同一個細胞 , 我沒有提到它 , 但它們看起來就像一個細胞 , 我還沒提到它 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義視覺影像的視覺影像 , 所以你可以想像一下 , 當你在這個影像時 , 你就可以想像發生在哪裡 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代的神經元 , 我們開始了解心理學過程 , 像是你記得或想像 , 或甚至認為 , 人類的神經元在數十億個體內的神經元中 , 會形成我們的大腦 。

imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全的機制 , 政府和公共衛生 , 不只不過是詹姆斯•史林斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•史蒂斯•斯特林斯的歷史 , 來解釋我們未來的未來應該要建立橋樑和公共 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、社群媒體、暴力、和平、政治、社群媒體、暴力等等 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•辛蒂: 「 詹姆斯•史蒂斯 」 : 「 詹姆斯蒂姆斯 」 的主題是: 「 世界安全 」 的主題 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談的是開放原始碼 , 因為我們必須在21世紀中更安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我開始說 , 咱們來回20世紀 , 來看看我們的生活方式如何運作 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是在法國北部 , 在法國的北部 , 在法國的北部 , 一個戰場 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年 , 大約200000000000000000000000000000000000000000萬人被殺死
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它轉移到20世紀的安全 , 二百萬人死了 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建立牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們走進一個寒戰戰爭的戰爭中 , 第二次世界大戰結束時 , 我們走進冷戰 , 然後進入冷戰 , 然後進入冷戰 , 然後進入冷戰 , 然後進入冷戰 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	今天我們要建立橋樑 , 我們需要建立橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它在巴爾蘭和巴勒斯坦河流行的一部分是歐洲和巴爾蘭的大樓 , 它會談到如何 , 它在大樓上有巨大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	近幾十年來 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始 , 去看這些社區 , 開始 , 開始 , 來看看這些社區開始 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會建議 , 開放原始碼 , 公開關聯國際關係 , 與策略性溝通 , 與策略性溝通 , 在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談一下為什麼我們需要這樣做 , 因為我們的全球公共公共公共公共公共公共公共公共公共公共公共公共公路 , 不必要做這個 。
